In the <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a>, it has been estimated that <a href="/wiki/Sauropod" class="mw-redirect" title="Sauropod">sauropods</a> could have emitted 520 million tons of methane to the atmosphere annually,<sup id="cite_ref-Wilkinson_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilkinson-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> contributing to the warmer climate of the time (up to 10&#160;°C warmer than at present).<sup id="cite_ref-Wilkinson_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilkinson-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sauropod_methane_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sauropod_methane-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> This large emission follows from the enormous estimated biomass of sauropods, and because methane production of individual herbivores is believed to be almost proportional to their mass.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilkinson_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilkinson-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recent studies have indicated that the extinction of megafaunal herbivores may have caused a reduction in <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_methane" title="Atmospheric methane">atmospheric methane</a>. This hypothesis is relatively new.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> One study examined the methane emissions from the <a href="/wiki/American_bison" title="American bison">bison</a> that occupied the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> of North America before contact with European settlers. The study estimated that the removal of the bison caused a decrease of as much as 2.2 million tons per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Kelliher_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kelliher-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Another study examined the change in the methane concentration in the atmosphere at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene_epoch" class="mw-redirect" title="Pleistocene epoch">Pleistocene epoch</a> after the extinction of megafauna in the Americas. After early humans migrated to the Americas about 13,000 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a>, their hunting and other associated ecological impacts led to the extinction of many megafaunal species there. Calculations suggest that this extinction decreased methane production by about 9.6 million tons per year. This suggests that the absence of megafaunal methane emissions may have contributed to the abrupt climatic cooling at the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Younger_Dryas" title="Younger Dryas">Younger Dryas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The decrease in atmospheric methane that occurred at that time, as recorded in <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">ice cores</a>, was 2–4 times more rapid than any other decrease in the last half million years, suggesting that an unusual mechanism was at work.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disease">Disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The hyperdisease hypothesis, proposed by Ross MacPhee in 1997, states that the megafaunal die-off was due to an indirect transmission of diseases by newly arriving <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">aboriginal humans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MacPhee&amp;Marx1997_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacPhee&amp;Marx1997-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MacPhee&amp;Marx1998_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacPhee&amp;Marx1998-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> According to MacPhee, aboriginals or animals travelling with them, such as <a href="/wiki/Domestic_dog" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic dog">domestic dogs</a> or livestock, introduced one or more highly <a href="/wiki/Virulent" class="mw-redirect" title="Virulent">virulent</a> diseases into new environments whose native population had no immunity to them, eventually leading to their extinction. <a href="/wiki/K-selection" class="mw-redirect" title="K-selection">K-selection</a> animals, such as the now-extinct megafauna, are especially vulnerable to diseases, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/R-selection" class="mw-redirect" title="R-selection">r-selection</a> animals who have a shorter <a href="/wiki/Gestation_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Gestation period">gestation period</a> and a higher population size. Humans are thought to be the sole cause as other earlier migrations of animals into North America from Eurasia did not cause extinctions.<sup id="cite_ref-MacPhee&amp;Marx1997_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacPhee&amp;Marx1997-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are many problems with this theory, as this disease would have to meet several criteria: it has to be able to sustain itself in an environment with no <a href="/wiki/Host_(biology)" title="Host (biology)">hosts</a>; it has to have a high <a href="/wiki/Infection_rate" title="Infection rate">infection rate</a>; and be extremely lethal, with a <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> of 50–75%. Disease has to be very virulent to kill off all the individuals in a <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">genus</a> or <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, and even such a virulent disease as <a href="/wiki/West_Nile_Virus" class="mw-redirect" title="West Nile Virus">West Nile Virus</a> is unlikely to have caused extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons_et_al2004_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons_et_al2004-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, diseases have been the cause for some extinctions. The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Avian_malaria" title="Avian malaria">avian malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avipoxvirus" title="Avipoxvirus">avipoxvirus</a>, for example, have had a negative impact on the <a href="/wiki/Endemic_birds_of_Hawaii" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic birds of Hawaii">endemic birds of Hawaii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LaPointe_2012_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaPointe_2012-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defaunation">Defaunation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Defaunation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Defaunation" title="Defaunation">Defaunation</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Susa_group,_mountain_gorilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg/220px-Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg/330px-Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg/440px-Susa_group%2C_mountain_gorilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1552" data-file-height="1632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Susa_group,_mountain_gorilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>There are roughly 880 <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorillas" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain gorillas">mountain gorillas</a> remaining in existence. 60% of <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primate</a> species face an anthropogenically driven extinction crisis and 75% have declining populations.<sup id="cite_ref-primates_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-primates-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The loss of species from ecological communities, defaunation, is primarily driven by human activity.<sup id="cite_ref-dirzo_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dirzo-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This has resulted in <a href="/wiki/Empty_forest" title="Empty forest">empty forests</a>, ecological communities depleted of large vertebrates.<sup id="cite_ref-primack2014_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-primack2014-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SpecialIssue_23-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpecialIssue-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This is not to be confused with extinction, as it includes both the disappearance of species and declines in abundance.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Defaunation effects were first implied at the Symposium of Plant-Animal Interactions at the University of Campinas, Brazil in 1988 in the context of <a href="/wiki/Neotropic_ecozone" class="mw-redirect" title="Neotropic ecozone">neotropical forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eco_and_evo_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco_and_evo-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Since then, the term has gained broader usage in conservation biology as a global phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-dirzo_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dirzo-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eco_and_evo_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco_and_evo-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Big_cat" title="Big cat">Big cat</a> populations have severely declined over the last half-century and could face extinction in the following decades. According to <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_the_Conservation_of_Nature" class="mw-redirect" title="International Union for the Conservation of Nature">IUCN</a> estimates: <a href="/wiki/Lions" class="mw-redirect" title="Lions">lions</a> are down to 25,000, from 450,000; <a href="/wiki/Leopards" class="mw-redirect" title="Leopards">leopards</a> are down to 50,000, from 750,000; <a href="/wiki/Cheetahs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cheetahs">cheetahs</a> are down to 12,000, from 45,000; <a href="/wiki/Tigers" class="mw-redirect" title="Tigers">tigers</a> are down to 3,000 in the wild, from 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-bigcats_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigcats-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> A December 2016 study by the Zoological Society of London, <a href="/wiki/Panthera_Corporation" title="Panthera Corporation">Panthera Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_Conservation_Society" title="Wildlife Conservation Society">Wildlife Conservation Society</a> showed that cheetahs are far closer to extinction than previously thought, with only 7,100 remaining in the wild, and crammed within only 9% of their historic range.<sup id="cite_ref-Visser_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visser-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Human pressures are to blame for the cheetah population crash, including prey loss due to overhunting by people, retaliatory killing from farmers, habitat loss and the illegal wildlife trade.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">We are seeing the effects of 7 billion people on the planet. At present rates, we will lose the big cats in 10 to 15 years.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>—&#8201;Naturalist Dereck Joubert, co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic</a> Big Cats Initiative<sup id="cite_ref-bigcats_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigcats-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The term <a href="/wiki/Pollinator_decline" title="Pollinator decline">pollinator decline</a> refers to the reduction in abundance of insect and other animal pollinators in many ecosystems worldwide beginning at the end of the twentieth century, and continuing into the present day.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Pollinators, which are necessary for 75% of food crops, are declining globally in both abundance and diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>  A 2017 study led by <a href="/wiki/Radboud_University_Nijmegen" title="Radboud University Nijmegen">Radboud University's</a> Hans de Kroon indicated that the biomass of insect life in Germany had declined by three-quarters in the previous 25 years.  Participating researcher Dave Goulson of <a href="/wiki/Sussex_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sussex University">Sussex University</a> stated that their study suggested that humans are making large parts of the planet uninhabitable for wildlife.  Goulson characterized the situation as an approaching "ecological Armageddon", adding that "if we lose the insects then everything is going to collapse."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">We have driven the rate of biological extinction, the permanent loss of species, up several hundred times beyond its historical levels, and are threatened with the loss of a majority of all species by the end of the 21st century.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>—&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Peter_H._Raven" title="Peter H. Raven">Peter Raven</a>, former president of the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a> (AAAS), in the foreword to their publication <i>AAAS Atlas of Population and Environment</i><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg/220px-Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg/330px-Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg/440px-Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2968" data-file-height="2152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_White_Rhinoceros_Angalifu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Angalifu_(rhinoceros)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angalifu (rhinoceros)">Angalifu</a>, a male <a href="/wiki/Northern_white_rhinoceros" title="Northern white rhinoceros">northern white rhinoceros</a> at the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Zoo_Safari_Park" title="San Diego Zoo Safari Park">San Diego Zoo Safari Park</a> (died December 2014).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(rhinoceros)" title="Sudan (rhinoceros)">Sudan</a>, the last male of the subspecies died on March 19, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Various species are predicted to <a href="/wiki/List_of_critically_endangered_species" class="mw-redirect" title="List of critically endangered species">become extinct in the near future</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> among them the <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> nonhuman <a href="/wiki/Primates" class="mw-redirect" title="Primates">primates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-primates_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-primates-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pangolins" class="mw-redirect" title="Pangolins">pangolins</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Giraffes" class="mw-redirect" title="Giraffes">giraffes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-suttergiraffe_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suttergiraffe-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">Hunting</a> alone threatens bird and mammalian populations around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Some scientists and academics assert that <a href="/wiki/Intensive_animal_farming" title="Intensive animal farming">industrial agriculture</a> and the growing demand for <a href="/wiki/Meat#Environmental_impact" title="Meat">meat</a> is contributing to significant global <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a> as this is a significant driver of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> and habitat destruction; species-rich habitats, such as significant portions of the Amazon region, are being converted to agriculture for meat production.<sup id="cite_ref-Zalasiewicz2015_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zalasiewicz2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> A 2017 study by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> (WWF) found that 60% of biodiversity loss can be attributed to the vast scale of feed crop cultivation required to rear tens of billions of farm animals.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, a 2006 report by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO) of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Livestock%27s_Long_Shadow" title="Livestock&#39;s Long Shadow">Livestock's Long Shadow</a></i>, also found that the livestock sector is a "leading player" in biodiversity loss.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> According to the WWF's 2016 <a href="/wiki/Living_Planet_Index" title="Living Planet Index">Living Planet Index</a>, global wildlife populations have declined 58% since 1970, primarily due to habitat destruction, over-hunting and pollution. They project that if current trends continue, 67% of wildlife could disappear by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> 189 countries, which are signatory to the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> (Rio Accord),<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> have committed to preparing a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Biodiversity Action Plan">Biodiversity Action Plan</a>, a first step at identifying specific <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a> and habitats, country by country.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">For the first time since the demise of the dinosaurs 65 million years ago, we face a global mass extinction of wildlife. We ignore the decline of other species at our peril – for they are the barometer that reveals our impact on the world that sustains us.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>—&#8201;Mike Barrett, director of science and policy at WWF's UK branch<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_extinction">Recent extinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Recent extinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List_extinct_in_the_wild_species" title="IUCN Red List extinct in the wild species">IUCN Red List extinct in the wild species</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_endangered_species" class="mw-redirect" title="List of endangered species">List of endangered species</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_critically_endangered_species" class="mw-redirect" title="List of critically endangered species">List of critically endangered species</a></div>
<p>Recent extinctions are more directly attributable to human influences, whereas prehistoric extinctions can be attributed to other factors, such as global climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-ceballos_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceballos-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dirzo_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dirzo-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> (IUCN) characterises 'recent' extinction as those that have occurred past the cut-off point of 1500,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> and at least 875 species have gone extinct since that time and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Some species, such as the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A8re_David%27s_deer" title="Père David&#39;s deer">Père David's deer</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_crow" title="Hawaiian crow">Hawaiian crow</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> are extinct in the wild, and survive solely in captive populations. Other species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Florida_panther" title="Florida panther">Florida panther</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Ecological_extinction" title="Ecological extinction">ecologically extinct</a>, surviving in such low numbers that they essentially have no impact on the ecosystem.<sup id="cite_ref-mckinney2013_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mckinney2013-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>318</span></sup> Other populations are only <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">locally extinct</a> (extirpated), still existence elsewhere, but reduced in distribution,<sup id="cite_ref-mckinney2013_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mckinney2013-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>75–77</span></sup> as with the extinction of <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whales</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and of the <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherback sea turtle</a> in Malaysia.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habitat_destruction">Habitat destruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Habitat destruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Extinction_risk_from_global_warming" title="Extinction risk from global warming">Extinction risk from global warming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">Ocean acidification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_pollution" title="Marine pollution">Marine pollution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_and_environmental_impact_of_palm_oil" title="Social and environmental impact of palm oil">Social and environmental impact of palm oil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/250px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/375px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/500px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of rainforest converted to <a href="/wiki/Oil_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil palm">oil palm</a> plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Global warming is widely accepted as being a contributor to extinction worldwide, in a similar way that <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">previous extinction events</a> have generally included a rapid change in global climate and meteorology. It is also expected to disrupt sex ratios in many reptiles which have <a href="/wiki/Temperature-dependent_sex_determination" title="Temperature-dependent sex determination">temperature-dependent sex determination</a>. 
</p><p>The removal of land to clear way for <a href="/wiki/Social_and_environmental_impact_of_palm_oil" title="Social and environmental impact of palm oil">palm oil plantations</a> releases carbon emissions held in the <a href="/wiki/Peatland" class="mw-redirect" title="Peatland">peatlands</a> of Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Foster_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foster-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_NYT_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal_NYT-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">Palm oil</a> mainly serves as a cheap <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and also as a (<a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">controversial</a>) <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>. However, damage to peatland contributes to 4% of global greenhouse gas emissions, and 8% of those caused by burning <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Palm oil cultivation has also been criticized for other impacts to the environment,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Greenpeace_Cooking_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace_Cooking-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> including deforestation,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> which has threatened critically endangered species such as the <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a><sup id="cite_ref-cspi_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cspi-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mail_Online_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mail_Online-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Tree-kangaroo" title="Tree-kangaroo">tree-kangaroo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The IUCN stated in 2016 that the species could go extinct within a decade if measures are not taken to preserve the rainforests in which they live.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rising levels of carbon dioxide are resulting in influx of this gas into the ocean, increasing its acidity. Marine organisms which possess <a href="/wiki/Seashell" title="Seashell">calcium carbonate shells</a> or <a href="/wiki/Exoskeleton" title="Exoskeleton">exoskeletons</a> experience physiological pressure as the carbonate reacts with acid. For example, this is already resulting in <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a> on various <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> worldwide, which provide valuable habitat and maintain a high biodiversity. Marine <a href="/wiki/Gastropod" class="mw-redirect" title="Gastropod">gastropods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bivalve" class="mw-redirect" title="Bivalve">bivalves</a> and other invertebrates are also affected, as are the organisms that feed on them.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> According to a 2018 study published in <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>, global <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" title="Killer whale">Orca</a> populations are poised to collapse due to toxic chemical and <a href="/wiki/Polychlorinated_biphenyl" title="Polychlorinated biphenyl">PCB</a> pollution. PCBs are still leaking into the sea in spite of being banned for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>  
</p><p>Some researchers suggest that by 2050 there could be more <a href="/wiki/Plastic_pollution" title="Plastic pollution">plastic</a> than fish in the oceans by weight,<sup id="cite_ref-Sutter_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sutter-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> with about 8,800,000 metric tons (9,700,000 short tons) of plastic being discharged into the oceans annually.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disposable_product" title="Disposable product">Single-use plastics</a>, such as plastic shopping bags, make up the bulk of this, and can often be ingested by marine life, such as with sea turtles.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> These plastics can degrade into <a href="/wiki/Microplastic" class="mw-redirect" title="Microplastic">microplastics</a>, smaller particles that can affect a larger array of species. Microplastics make up the bulk of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Pacific_Garbage_Patch" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Pacific Garbage Patch">Great Pacific Garbage Patch</a>, and their smaller size is detrimental to cleanup efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overexploitation">Overexploitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Overexploitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Species_affected_by_poaching" title="Species affected by poaching">Species affected by poaching</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">Overfishing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg/220px-Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg/330px-Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg/440px-Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1811" data-file-height="890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaquita4_Olson_NOAA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Vaquita" title="Vaquita">vaquita</a>, the world's most endangered marine mammal, has been reduced to only 30 individuals as of February 2017. They are often killed by commercial fishing nets.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2018, only 12 remain, according to The International Committee for the Recovery of the Vaquita.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg/220px-Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg/330px-Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg/440px-Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="942" data-file-height="738" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Surexploitation_morue_surp%C3%AAcheEn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The collapse of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_cod" title="Atlantic cod">Atlantic cod</a> off the coast of Newfoundland in 1992 as a result of <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Overhunting can reduce the local population of <a href="/wiki/Game_(hunting)" title="Game (hunting)">game animals</a> by more than half, as well as reducing population density, and may lead to extinction for some species.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Populations located nearer to villages are significantly more at risk of depletion.<sup id="cite_ref-peres2006_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peres2006-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Several conservationist organizations, among them <a href="/wiki/IFAW" class="mw-redirect" title="IFAW">IFAW</a> and <a href="/wiki/HSUS" class="mw-redirect" title="HSUS">HSUS</a>, assert that <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">trophy hunters</a>, particularly from the United States, are playing a significant role in the decline of giraffes, which they refer to as a "silent extinction".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The surge in the mass killings by <a href="/wiki/Poachers" class="mw-redirect" title="Poachers">poachers</a> involved in the illegal ivory trade along with habitat loss is threatening <a href="/wiki/African_elephant" title="African elephant">African elephant</a> populations.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sevenyears_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sevenyears-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, their populations stood at 1.7 million; at present there are fewer than 400,000 remaining.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Prior to European colonization, scientists believe Africa was home to roughly 20 million elephants.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Elephant_Census" title="Great Elephant Census">Great Elephant Census</a>, 30% of African elephants (or 144,000 individuals) disappeared over a seven-year period, 2007 to 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-sevenyears_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sevenyears-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> African elephants could become extinct by 2035 if poaching rates continue.<sup id="cite_ref-suttergiraffe_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suttergiraffe-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fishing has had a devastating effect on marine organism populations for several centuries even before the explosion of destructive and highly effective fishing practices like <a href="/wiki/Trawling" title="Trawling">trawling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Humans are unique among predators in that they regularly predate on other adult <a href="/wiki/Apex_predator" title="Apex predator">apex predators</a>, particularly in marine environments;<sup id="cite_ref-:4_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bluefin_tuna" title="Bluefin tuna">bluefin tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue whales">blue whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic right whales">North Atlantic right whales</a><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> and various <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharks</a> in particular are particularly vulnerable to predation pressure from human fishing. A 2016 study published in <i>Science</i> concludes that humans tend to hunt larger species, and this could disrupt ocean ecosystems for millions of years.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">If this pattern goes unchecked, the future oceans would lack many of the largest species in today’s oceans. Many large species play critical roles in ecosystems and so their extinctions could lead to ecological cascades that would influence the structure and function of future ecosystems beyond the simple fact of losing those species.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>—&#8201;Jonathan Payne, associate professor and chair of geological sciences at Stanford University<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disease_2">Disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_amphibian_populations" title="Decline in amphibian populations">Decline in amphibian populations</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_nose_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="White nose syndrome">White nose syndrome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colony_collapse_disorder" title="Colony collapse disorder">Colony collapse disorder</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bufo_periglenes2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bufo_periglenes2.jpg/220px-Bufo_periglenes2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bufo_periglenes2.jpg/330px-Bufo_periglenes2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bufo_periglenes2.jpg/440px-Bufo_periglenes2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3576" data-file-height="2385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bufo_periglenes2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Golden_toad" title="Golden toad">golden toad</a> of Costa Rica, extinct since around 1989. Its disappearance has been attributed to a confluence of several factors, including <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> warming, fungus, habitat loss and the introduction of invasive species.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg/220px-Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg/330px-Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg/440px-Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecnomiohyla_rabborum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Toughie_(frog)" title="Toughie (frog)">Toughie</a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Rabbs%27_fringe-limbed_treefrog" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabbs&#39; fringe-limbed treefrog">Rabbs' fringe-limbed treefrog</a>, died in September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The species was killed off from the <a href="/wiki/Chytrid_fungus" class="mw-redirect" title="Chytrid fungus">chytrid fungus</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Batrachochytrium_dendrobatidis" title="Batrachochytrium dendrobatidis">Batrachochytrium dendrobatidis</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The decline of amphibian populations has also been identified as an indicator of environmental degradation. As well as habitat loss, introduced predators and pollution, <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycosis" title="Chytridiomycosis">Chytridiomycosis</a>, a fungal infection thought to have been accidentally spread by human travel,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> has caused severe population drops of several species of frogs, including (among many others) the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_toad" title="Golden toad">golden toad</a> in Costa Rica and the <a href="/wiki/Gastric-brooding_frog" title="Gastric-brooding frog">Gastric-brooding frog</a> in Australia. Many other amphibian species now face extinction, including the reduction of <a href="/wiki/Rabb%27s_Fringe-limbed_Treefrog" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabb&#39;s Fringe-limbed Treefrog">Rabb's fringe-limbed treefrog</a> to an <a href="/wiki/Endling" title="Endling">endling</a>, and the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Panamanian_golden_frog" title="Panamanian golden frog">Panamanian golden frog</a> in the wild. Chytrid fungus has spread across Australia, New Zealand, Central America and Africa, including countries with high amphibian diversity such as <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">cloud forests</a> in <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Batrachochytrium_salamandrivorans" title="Batrachochytrium salamandrivorans">Batrachochytrium salamandrivorans</a></i> is a similar infection currently threatening <a href="/wiki/Salamander" title="Salamander">salamanders</a>. Amphibians are now the most endangered vertebrate group, having existed for more than 300 million years through three other <a href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass extinction">mass extinctions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>17</span></sup>
</p><p>Millions of bats in the US have been dying off since 2012 due to a fungal infection spread from European bats, which appear to be immune. Population drops have been as great as 90% within five years, and extinction of at least one bat species is predicted. There is currently no form of treatment, and such declines have been described as "unprecedented" in bat evolutionary history by Alan Hicks of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Department_of_Environmental_Conservation" title="New York State Department of Environmental Conservation">New York State Department of Environmental Conservation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 2007 and 2013, over ten million beehives were abandoned due to <a href="/wiki/Colony_collapse_disorder" title="Colony collapse disorder">colony collapse disorder</a>, which causes <a href="/wiki/Worker_bee" title="Worker bee">worker bees</a> to abandon the <a href="/wiki/Queen_bee" title="Queen bee">queen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> This disorder has been attributed to - amongst other things - <a href="/wiki/Neonicotinoid" title="Neonicotinoid">neonicotinoids</a> consumed by worker bees from the extensive use of pesticides in human farming methods.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mitigation">Mitigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mitigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some leading scientists have advocated for the global community to designate as protected areas 30 percent of the planet by 2030, and 50 percent by 2050, in order to mitigate the contemporary extinction crisis as the human population is projected to grow to 10 billion by the middle of the century. Human consumption of food and water resources is also projected to double by this time.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Holocene_extinction&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

"Effect of per-capita land use changes on Holocene forest clearance and CO<sub>2</sub> emissions". <i>Quaternary Science Reviews</i>. <b>28</b> (27–28): 3011–3015. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">Bibcode</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2009QSRv...28.3011R">2009QSRv...28.3011R</a>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.quascirev.2009.05.022">10.1016/j.quascirev.2009.05.022</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Quaternary+Science+Reviews&amp;rft.atitle=Effect+of+per-capita+land+use+changes+on+Holocene+forest+clearance+and+CO%3Csub%3E2%3C%2Fsub%3E+emissions&amp;rft.volume=28&amp;rft.issue=27%E2%80%9328&amp;rft.pages=3011-3015&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.quascirev.2009.05.022&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2009QSRv...28.3011R&amp;rft.aulast=Ruddiman&amp;rft.aufirst=W.F.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHolocene+extinction" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a href="/wiki/Yuval_Noah_Harari" title="Yuval Noah Harari">Harari, Yuval N.</a> (September 25, 2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2015/sep/25/industrial-farming-one-worst-crimes-history-ethical-question">"Industrial farming is one of the worst crimes in history"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 23,</span> 2016</span>. <q>Even tens of thousands of years ago, our stone age ancestors were already responsible for a series of ecological disasters. When the first humans reached Australia about 45,000 years ago, they quickly drove to extinction 90% of its large animals. This was the first significant impact that <i>Homo sapiens</i> had on the planet’s <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a>. It was not the last. About 15,000 years ago, humans colonised America, wiping out in the process about 75% of its large mammals. Numerous other species disappeared from Africa, from Eurasia and from the myriad islands around their coasts.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Guardian&amp;rft.atitle=Industrial+farming+is+one+of+the+worst+crimes+in+history&amp;rft.date=2015-09-25&amp;rft.aulast=Harari&amp;rft.aufirst=Yuval+N.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.theguardian.com%2Fbooks%2F2015%2Fsep%2F25%2Findustrial-farming-one-worst-crimes-history-ethical-question&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHolocene+extinction" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
